</p><p>Historically, the party has represented farmers, laborers, labor unions and religious and ethnic minorities as it has opposed unregulated business and finance and favored progressive income taxes. In foreign policy, <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">internationalism</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Interventionism_(politics)" title="Interventionism (politics)">interventionism</a>) was a dominant theme from 1913 to the mid-1960s. In the 1930s, the party began advocating <a href="/wiki/Social_programs_in_the_United_States" title="Social programs in the United States">welfare</a> spending programs targeted at the poor. The party had a <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_conservatism" title="Fiscal conservatism">fiscally conservative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">pro-business</a> wing, typified by <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Smith" title="Al Smith">Al Smith</a>; and a <a href="/wiki/Southern_Democrats" title="Southern Democrats">Southern</a> conservative wing that shrank after President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> supported the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>. The major influences for liberalism were labor unions (which peaked in the 1936–1952 era) and the <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> wing, which has steadily grown since the 1960s. Since the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> has been a major new component.
</p><p>The Democratic Party, once dominant in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">Southeastern United States</a>, is now strongest in the Northeast (<a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Mid-Atlantic States">Mid-Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>), <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region_(North_America)" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Lakes region (North America)">Great Lakes region</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">West Coast</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>). The Democrats are also very strong in <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">major cities</a> (regardless of region).
</p><p>Social scientists Theodore Caplow et al. argue that "the Democratic party, nationally, moved from left-center toward the center in the 1940s and 1950s, then moved further toward the right-center in the 1970s and 1980s".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> According to historian <a href="/wiki/Walter_Scheidel" title="Walter Scheidel">Walter Scheidel</a>, both major political parties shifted towards promoting <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a> in the 1970s, with Republicans moving further to the political right than Democrats to the political left. He contends Democrats played a significant role in the financial deregulation of the 1990s and have pushed social welfare issues to the periphery while increasingly focusing on issues pertaining to <a href="/wiki/Identity_politics" title="Identity politics">identity politics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Centrists">Centrists</span></h3>
<p>Centrist Democrats, or <a href="/wiki/New_Democrats" title="New Democrats">New Democrats</a>, are an ideologically <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a> faction within the Democratic Party that emerged after the victory of <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1988_United_States_presidential_election" title="1988 United States presidential election">1988 presidential election</a>. They are an economically <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">liberal</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Third_Way" title="Third Way">Third Way</a>" faction which dominated the party for around 20 years starting in the late 1980s after the United States populace turned much further to the <a href="/wiki/Political_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Political right">political right</a>. They are represented by organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/New_Democrat_Network" title="New Democrat Network">New Democrat Network</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_Democrat_Coalition" title="New Democrat Coalition">New Democrat Coalition</a>.
</p><p>The New Democrat Coalition is a pro-business, pro-growth and <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_conservatism" title="Fiscal conservatism">fiscally conservative</a> congressional coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Compared to other Democratic factions, they are mostly more supportive of the use of military force, including the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">war in Iraq</a>, are more supportive of <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> and are more willing to reduce government welfare as indicated by their support for <a href="/wiki/Welfare_reform" title="Welfare reform">welfare reform</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tax_cut" title="Tax cut">tax cuts</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>One of the most influential centrist groups was the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Leadership_Council" title="Democratic Leadership Council">Democratic Leadership Council</a> (DLC), a nonprofit organization that advocated centrist positions for the party. The DLC hailed President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> as proof of the viability of "Third Way" politicians and a DLC success story. The DLC disbanded in 2011 and much of the former DLC is now represented in the think tank <a href="/wiki/Third_Way_(United_States)" title="Third Way (United States)">Third Way</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While not representing a majority of the Democratic Party electorate, a decent amount of Democratic elected officials have self-declared as being centrists. Some of these Democrats are former President Bill Clinton, former Vice President <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, Senator <a href="/wiki/Mark_Warner" title="Mark Warner">Mark Warner</a>, former Pennsylvania governor <a href="/wiki/Ed_Rendell" title="Ed Rendell">Ed Rendell</a>, former senator <a href="/wiki/Jim_Webb" title="Jim Webb">Jim Webb</a>, Vice President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>, congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Ann_Kirkpatrick" title="Ann Kirkpatrick">Ann Kirkpatrick</a> and former congressman <a href="/wiki/Dave_McCurdy" title="Dave McCurdy">Dave McCurdy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Members_-_New_Democrat_Coalition_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Members_-_New_Democrat_Coalition-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The New Democrat Network supports socially moderate, fiscally conservative Democratic politicians and operates the congressional <a href="/wiki/New_Democrat_Coalition" title="New Democrat Coalition">New Democrat Coalition</a> in the House and Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Congressman <a href="/wiki/Ron_Kind" title="Ron Kind">Ron Kind</a> is the chairperson of the coalition<sup id="cite_ref-Members_-_New_Democrat_Coalition_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Members_-_New_Democrat_Coalition-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and former senator and 2016 Democratic presidential nominee <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> was a member while in Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Before he became President, Senator <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was self-described as a New Democrat.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservatives">Conservatives</span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Democrat" title="Conservative Democrat">conservative Democrat</a> is a member of the Democratic Party with <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a> political views, or with views relatively conservative with respect to those of the national party. While such members of the Democratic Party can be found throughout the nation, actual elected officials are disproportionately found within the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern states</a> and to a lesser extent within <a href="/wiki/Rural_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural United States">rural</a> regions of the United States generally, more commonly in the <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">West</a>. Historically, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Democrats" title="Southern Democrats">Southern Democrats</a> were generally much more ideologically conservative than conservative Democrats are now.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg/220px-State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg/330px-State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg/440px-State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="894" data-file-height="501" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:State_Dining_Room_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> meeting with the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Dog_Coalition" title="Blue Dog Coalition">Blue Dog Coalition</a> in the <a href="/wiki/State_Dining_Room_of_the_White_House" title="State Dining Room of the White House">State Dining Room of the White House</a> in 2009.</div></div></div>
<p>Many conservative Southern Democrats defected to the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>, beginning with the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a> and the general leftward shift of the party. <a href="/wiki/Strom_Thurmond" title="Strom Thurmond">Strom Thurmond</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Tauzin" title="Billy Tauzin">Billy Tauzin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kent_Hance" title="Kent Hance">Kent Hance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Hall" title="Ralph Hall">Ralph Hall</a> of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Shelby" title="Richard Shelby">Richard Shelby</a> of <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> are examples of this. The influx of conservative Democrats into the Republican Party is often cited as a reason for the Republican Party's shift further to the right during the late 20th century as well as the shift of its base from the Northeast and Midwest to the South.
</p><p>Into the 1980s, the Democratic Party had a conservative element, mostly from the South and Border regions. Their numbers declined sharply as the Republican Party built up its Southern base. They were sometimes humorously called "<a href="/wiki/Yellow_dog_Democrat" title="Yellow dog Democrat">Yellow dog Democrats</a>", or "<a href="/wiki/Boll_weevil_(politics)" title="Boll weevil (politics)">boll weevils</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dixiecrats" class="mw-redirect" title="Dixiecrats">Dixiecrats</a>". In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House</a>, they form the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Dog_Coalition" title="Blue Dog Coalition">Blue Dog Coalition</a>, a caucus of <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_conservatism" title="Fiscal conservatism">fiscal conservatives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_conservatism" title="Social conservatism">social conservatives</a> and moderates, primarily Southerners, willing to broker compromises with the Republican leadership. They have acted as a unified voting bloc in the past, giving its members some ability to change legislation, depending on their numbers in Congress.
</p><p>There was a split vote among many conservative Southern Democrats in the 1970s and 1980s. Some supported local and statewide conservative Democrats while simultaneously voting for Republican presidential candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberals">Liberals</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">Modern liberalism in the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago,_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago%2C_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg/220px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago%2C_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago%2C_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg/330px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago%2C_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago%2C_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg/440px-Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago%2C_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2083" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eleanor_Roosevelt_at_the_Democratic_Nationall_Convention_in_Chicago,_Illinois_-_NARA_-_195997.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1956_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1956 Democratic National Convention">1956 Democratic National Convention</a> in Chicago</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">Social liberals</a> (modern liberals) and <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressives</a> constitute the majority of the Democratic voter base. Liberals thereby form the largest united demographic within the Democratic base. According to the 2012 exit poll results, liberals constituted 25% of the electorate, and 86% of American liberals favored the candidate of the Democratic Party.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">White-collar</a> college-educated professionals were mostly Republican until the 1950s, but they now compose a vital component of the Democratic Party.<sup id="cite_ref-Judis,_B._J._(July_11,_2003)._The_trouble_with_Howard_Dean._&#39;&#39;Salon.com&#39;&#39;._104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judis,_B._J._(July_11,_2003)._The_trouble_with_Howard_Dean._&#39;&#39;Salon.com&#39;&#39;.-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A large majority of liberals favor moving toward <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>, with many supporting a <a href="/wiki/Single-payer_health_care" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-payer health care">single-payer system</a>. A majority also favor <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a> over <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">military action</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell research</a>, the legalization of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>, stricter <a href="/wiki/Gun_politics_in_the_United_States" title="Gun politics in the United States">gun control</a> and environmental protection laws as well as the preservation of <a href="/wiki/Pro-choice" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-choice">abortion rights</a>. Immigration and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_diversity" title="Cultural diversity">cultural diversity</a> is deemed positive as liberals favor <a href="/wiki/Cultural_pluralism" title="Cultural pluralism">cultural pluralism</a>, a system in which immigrants retain their native culture in addition to adopting their new culture. They tend to be divided on <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) and organizations, with some seeing them as more favorable to corporations than workers. Most liberals oppose increased military spending and the mixing of church and state.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Research_Center._105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Research_Center.-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This ideological group differs from the traditional organized labor base. According to the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, a plurality of 41% resided in <a href="/wiki/Mass_affluent" title="Mass affluent">mass affluent</a> households and 49% were college graduates, the highest figure of any typographical group. It was also the fastest growing typological group between the late 1990s and early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Research_Center._105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Research_Center.-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Liberals include most of academia<sup id="cite_ref-Kurtz,_H._(March_29,_2005)._College_Faculties_A_Most_Liberal_Lot,_Study_Finds._&#39;&#39;The_Washington_Post&#39;&#39;._106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kurtz,_H._(March_29,_2005)._College_Faculties_A_Most_Liberal_Lot,_Study_Finds._&#39;&#39;The_Washington_Post&#39;&#39;.-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> and large portions of the professional class.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN._(2000)._Exit_Poll._90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN._(2000)._Exit_Poll.-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN._(2004)._Exit_Poll._91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN._(2004)._Exit_Poll.-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN._(2006)._Exit_Poll._92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN._(2006)._Exit_Poll.-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Progressives">Progressives</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_Warren,_official_portrait,_114th_Congress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Elizabeth_Warren%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg/200px-Elizabeth_Warren%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Elizabeth_Warren%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg/300px-Elizabeth_Warren%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Elizabeth_Warren%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg/400px-Elizabeth_Warren%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1908" data-file-height="2385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_Warren,_official_portrait,_114th_Congress.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Progressivism_in_the_United_States" title="Progressivism in the United States">Progressives</a> are the most left-leaning, pro-<a href="/wiki/Labor_unions_in_the_United_States" title="Labor unions in the United States">labor union</a> faction in the party who have long supported a strong regulation of business, <a href="/wiki/Social_programs_in_the_United_States" title="Social programs in the United States">social-welfare programs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Workers&#39; rights">workers' rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Many progressive Democrats are descendants of the <a href="/wiki/New_Left" title="New Left">New Left</a> of Democratic presidential candidate Senator <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">George McGovern</a> of South Dakota whereas others were involved in the <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders_presidential_campaign,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernie Sanders presidential campaign, 2016">2016 presidential candidacy</a> of Vermont Senator <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a>.
</p><p>In 2014, progressive Senator <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a> set out an "Eleven Commandments of Progressivism", being tougher regulation on corporations, affordable education, scientific investment and <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality" title="Net neutrality">net neutrality</a>, increased wages, equal pay, collective bargaining rights, defending social safety-net programs, marriage equality, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_reform_in_the_US" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration reform in the US">immigration reform</a> and unabridged access to reproductive healthcare.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, progressives strongly oppose <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">political corruption</a> and therefore seek to advance electoral reform including campaign finance reform and voting rights.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Today, many progressives have made a fight against <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality_in_the_united_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic inequality in the united states">economic inequality</a> their top priority.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Progressives are generally considered to be synonymous with liberals, though the two groups differ on a variety of issues,<sup id="cite_ref-huffingtonpost.com_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> such as progressives' stronger support for universal healthcare, solutions for economic inequality, and stronger environmental regulations. Progressives tend to be seen as closer to the ideology of European <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a> parties than mainstream or establishment liberals.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Progressive_Caucus" title="Congressional Progressive Caucus">Congressional Progressive Caucus</a> is a caucus of progressive Democrats and is the single largest Democratic caucus in the House of Representatives. Its current chairs are <a href="/wiki/Mark_Pocan" title="Mark Pocan">Mark Pocan</a> of Wisconsin and <a href="/wiki/Pramila_Jayapal" title="Pramila Jayapal">Pramila Jayapal</a> of Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Its members have included Representatives <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Kucinich" title="Dennis Kucinich">Dennis Kucinich</a> of Ohio, <a href="/wiki/John_Conyers" title="John Conyers">John Conyers</a> of Michigan, <a href="/wiki/Jim_McDermott" title="Jim McDermott">Jim McDermott</a> of Washington, <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_(Georgia_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Lewis (Georgia politician)">John Lewis</a> of Georgia, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Lee" title="Barbara Lee">Barbara Lee</a> of California and the late Senator <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wellstone" title="Paul Wellstone">Paul Wellstone</a> of Minnesota. Senators <a href="/wiki/Sherrod_Brown" title="Sherrod Brown">Sherrod Brown</a> of Ohio, <a href="/wiki/Tammy_Baldwin" title="Tammy Baldwin">Tammy Baldwin</a> of Wisconsin, <a href="/wiki/Mazie_Hirono" title="Mazie Hirono">Mazie Hirono</a> of Hawaii and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Markey" title="Ed Markey">Ed Markey</a> of Massachusetts were all members of the caucus when in the House of Representatives. Today, no Democratic Senators belong to the Progressive Caucus, but independent Senator Bernie Sanders is a member.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_positions">Political positions</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_positions_of_the_Democratic_Party" title="Political positions of the Democratic Party">Political positions of the Democratic Party</a></div>
<dl><dt>Economic policy</dt>
<dd></dd></dl>
<ul><li>Expand <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">social security</a> and safety net programs.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Increase top <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax_in_the_United_States" title="Capital gains tax in the United States">capital gains tax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dividend_tax" title="Dividend tax">dividend tax</a> rates to above 28%.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Across the board tax-cuts for the low and middle class and small businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Change tax rules to not encourage shipping jobs overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Increase federal and state <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_the_United_States" title="Minimum wage in the United States">minimum wages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Modernize and expand access to <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States" title="Education in the United States">public education</a> and provide <a href="/wiki/Universal_preschool" title="Universal preschool">universal preschool</a> education.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cpc.grijalva.house.gov_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpc.grijalva.house.gov-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Support for <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Greater investment in <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> development.<sup id="cite_ref-cpc.grijalva.house.gov_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpc.grijalva.house.gov-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Increase investments in scientific and technological research and development.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Expand the use of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> and diminish the use of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Implement a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_tax" title="Carbon tax">carbon tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Uphold labor protections and the right to <a href="/wiki/Labor_unions_in_the_United_States" title="Labor unions in the United States">unionize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Reform the <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_the_United_States" title="Student loans in the United States">student loan</a> system and allow for refinancing student loans.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Expand <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free college</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Mandate <a href="/wiki/Equal_pay_for_equal_work" title="Equal pay for equal work">equal pay for equal work</a> regardless of gender, race, or ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<dl><dt>Social policy</dt>
<dd></dd></dl>
<ul><li>Decriminalization or legalization of marijuana.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Uphold <a href="/wiki/Network_neutrality_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Network neutrality in the United States">network neutrality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Implement <a href="/wiki/Campaign_finance_reform_in_the_United_States" title="Campaign finance reform in the United States">campaign finance reform</a> and electoral reform.<sup id="cite_ref-ontheissues.org_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ontheissues.org-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Uphold <a href="/wiki/Voting_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Voting rights">voting rights</a> and easy access to voting.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Support for <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_union_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil union in the United States">civil unions</a>. Bans on <a href="/wiki/Conversion_therapy" title="Conversion therapy">conversion therapy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_118-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Allow legal access to <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_United_States" title="Abortion in the United States">abortions</a> and women's reproductive health care.</li>
<li>Reform the immigration system and allow for a <a href="/wiki/Immigration_reform_in_the_United_States" title="Immigration reform in the United States">pathway to citizenship</a>.</li>
<li>Support for gun background checks and stricter <a href="/wiki/Gun_control" title="Gun control">gun control</a> regulations.</li>
<li>Improve privacy laws and curtail government surveillance.</li>
<li>Opposition to the use of <a href="/wiki/Torture_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Torture in the United States">torture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Recognize and defend <a href="/wiki/Internet_freedom" title="Internet freedom">Internet freedom</a> worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_issues">Economic issues</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Equal_opportunity_employment" class="mw-redirect" title="Equal opportunity employment">Equal economic opportunity</a>, a base <a href="/wiki/Social_safety_net" title="Social safety net">social safety net</a> provided by the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> and strong <a href="/wiki/Labor_unions_in_the_United_States" title="Labor unions in the United States">labor unions</a> have historically been at the heart of Democratic economic policy.<sup id="cite_ref-Larry_E._Sullivan_2009_p_291_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_E._Sullivan_2009_p_291-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The welfare state supports a <a href="/wiki/Progressive_tax" title="Progressive tax">progressive tax</a> system, higher <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_the_United_States" title="Minimum wage in the United States">minimum wages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">social security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States" title="Education in the United States">public education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_housing_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Public housing in the United States">public housing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Larry_E._Sullivan_2009_p_291_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Larry_E._Sullivan_2009_p_291-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They also support <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> development and government-sponsored employment programs in an effort to achieve economic development and job creation while stimulating private sector job creation.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, since the 1990s the party has at times supported <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a> economic reforms, which cut the size of government and reduced market regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The party has continuously rejected <a href="/wiki/Laissez-faire" title="Laissez-faire"><i>laissez-faire</i> economics</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Market_socialism" title="Market socialism">market socialism</a>, instead favoring <a href="/wiki/Keynesian_economics" title="Keynesian economics">Keynesian economics</a> within a capitalist market-based system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiscal_policy">Fiscal policy</span></h4>
<p>Democrats support a more <a href="/wiki/Progressive_tax" title="Progressive tax">progressive tax</a> structure to provide more services and reduce <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">economic inequality</a> by making sure that the wealthiest Americans pay the highest amount in taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-how-high_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-how-high-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Democrats support more <a href="/wiki/Government_spending" title="Government spending">government spending</a> on social services while spending less on the military.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> They oppose the cutting of social services, such as <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)" title="Medicare (United States)">Medicare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicaid" title="Medicaid">Medicaid</a> and various other <a href="/wiki/Welfare_(financial_aid)" class="mw-redirect" title="Welfare (financial aid)">welfare</a> programs,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> believing it to be harmful to efficiency and <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>. Democrats believe the benefits of social services in monetary and non-monetary terms are a more <a href="/wiki/Productive_and_unproductive_labour" title="Productive and unproductive labour">productive labor</a> force and cultured population and believe that the benefits of this are greater than any benefits that could be derived from lower taxes, especially on top earners, or cuts to social services. Furthermore, Democrats see social services as essential towards providing <a href="/wiki/Positive_liberty" title="Positive liberty">positive freedom</a>, i.e. freedom derived from economic opportunity. The Democratic-led House of Representatives reinstated the <a href="/wiki/PAYGO" title="PAYGO">PAYGO</a> (pay-as-you-go) budget rule at the start of the <a href="/wiki/110th_United_States_Congress" title="110th United States Congress">110th Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minimum_wage">Minimum wage</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_minimum_wage" class="mw-redirect" title="United States minimum wage">United States minimum wage</a></div>
<p>The Democratic Party favors raising the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a>. They call for a $10.10/hour national minimum wage and think the minimum wage should be adjusted regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fair_Minimum_Wage_Act_of_2007" title="Fair Minimum Wage Act of 2007">Fair Minimum Wage Act of 2007</a> was an early component of the Democrats' agenda during the <a href="/wiki/110th_United_States_Congress" title="110th United States Congress">110th Congress</a>. In 2006, the Democrats supported six state ballot initiatives to increase the minimum wage and all six initiatives passed.<sup id="cite_ref-democrats.org_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-democrats.org-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In May 2017, Senate Democrats introduced the Raise the Wage Act which would raise the minimum wage to $15 an hour by 2024 and marks a leftward turn in Democratic economic policies.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg/220px-Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg/330px-Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg/440px-Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama_signing_health_care-20100323.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Barack Obama signing the <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act</a> into law at the White House on March 23, 2010</div></div></div>
<p>Democrats call for "affordable and quality health care" and many advocate an expansion of government intervention in this area. Many Democrats favor <a href="/wiki/National_health_insurance" title="National health insurance">national health insurance</a> or <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> in a variety of forms to address the rising costs of modern <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>. Some Democrats, such as former Representatives <a href="/wiki/John_Conyers" title="John Conyers">John Conyers</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dingell" title="John Dingell">John Dingell</a>, have called for a <a href="/wiki/Single-payer_health_care" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-payer health care">single-payer program</a> of <a href="/wiki/Medicare_for_All" class="mw-redirect" title="Medicare for All">Medicare for All</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democrats_of_America" title="Progressive Democrats of America">Progressive Democrats of America</a>, a group operating inside the Democratic Party, has made single-payer universal health care one of their primary policy goals.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act</a>, signed into law by President Obama on March 23, 2010, has been one of the most significant pushes for universal health care to become a reality. By April 2014, more than 10 million Americans had enrolled in health care coverage since the launch of the Affordable Care Act.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h4>
<p>Democrats favor improving <a href="/wiki/Public_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Public education">public education</a> by raising school standards and reforming the <a href="/wiki/Head_start_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Head start program">head start program</a>. They also support <a href="/wiki/Universal_preschool" title="Universal preschool">universal preschool</a> and expanding access to primary education, including through <a href="/wiki/Charter_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter schools">charter schools</a>. They call for slashes in <a href="/wiki/Student_loan" title="Student loan">student loan</a> debt and support reforms to force down tuition fees.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Other proposed reforms have included nationwide universal preschool education, tuition-free college and reform of <a href="/wiki/Standardized_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Standardized testing">standardized testing</a>. Democrats have the long-term aim of having low-cost, publicly funded college education with low tuition fees (like in much of Europe and Canada), which should be available to every eligible American student. Alternatively, they encourage expanding access to post-secondary education by increasing state funding for student financial aid such as <a href="/wiki/Pell_Grants" class="mw-redirect" title="Pell Grants">Pell Grants</a> and <a href="/wiki/College_tuition" class="mw-redirect" title="College tuition">college tuition</a> <a href="/wiki/Tax_deductions" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax deductions">tax deductions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy_of_the_United_States" title="Environmental policy of the United States">Environmental policy of the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_(26554283406).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_%2826554283406%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_%2826554283406%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_%2826554283406%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_%2826554283406%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_%2826554283406%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_%2826554283406%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4564" data-file-height="3043" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Addresses_Delegates_Before_Signing_the_COP21_Climate_Change_Agreement_on_Earth_Day_in_New_York_(26554283406).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> addresses delegates at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> before signing the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> on April 22, 2016.</div></div></div>
<p>Democrats believe that the government should protect the environment and have a history of <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>. In more recent years, this stance has had as its emphasis alternative energy generation as the basis for an improved economy, greater <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">national security</a> and general environmental benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Democratic Party also favors expansion of conservation lands and encourages open space and rail travel to relieve highway and airport congestion and improve air quality and economy as it "believe[s] that communities, environmental interests, and the government should work together to protect resources while ensuring the vitality of local economies. Once Americans were led to believe they had to make a choice between the economy and the environment. They now know this is a false choice".<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most important environmental concern of the Democratic Party is <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. Democrats, most notably former Vice President <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, have pressed for stern regulation of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>. On October 15, 2007, he won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for his efforts to build greater knowledge about man-made <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and laying the foundations for the measures needed to counteract these changes asserting that "the climate crisis is not a political issue, it is a moral and spiritual challenge to all of humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy_and_fossil_fuels">Renewable energy and fossil fuels</span></h4>
<p>Democrats have supported increased domestic <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> development, including wind and solar power farms, in an effort to reduce carbon pollution. The party's platform calls for an "all of the above" energy policy including clean energy, natural gas and domestic oil, with the desire of becoming energy independent.<sup id="cite_ref-democrats.org_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-democrats.org-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The party has supported higher taxes on <a href="/wiki/Oil_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil companies">oil companies</a> and increased regulations on <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal power plant">coal power plants</a>, favoring a policy of reducing long-term reliance on <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, the party supports stricter <a href="/wiki/Fuel_emissions_standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuel emissions standard">fuel emissions standards</a> to prevent air pollution.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_agreements">Trade agreements</span></h4>
<p>Many Democrats support <a href="/wiki/Fair_trade" title="Fair trade">fair trade</a> policies when it comes to the issue of <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a> agreements and some in the party have started supporting <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> in recent decades.<sup id="cite_ref-Rorty_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rorty-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the 1990s, the Clinton administration and a number of prominent Democrats pushed through a number of agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA). Since then, the party's shift away from free trade became evident in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_%E2%80%93_Central_America_Free_Trade_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominican Republic – Central America Free Trade Agreement">Central American Free Trade Agreement</a> (CAFTA) vote, with 15 House Democrats voting for the agreement and 187 voting against.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues">Social issues</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shirley_Chisholm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Shirley_Chisholm.jpg/220px-Shirley_Chisholm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Shirley_Chisholm.jpg/330px-Shirley_Chisholm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Shirley_Chisholm.jpg/440px-Shirley_Chisholm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3014" data-file-height="4492" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shirley_Chisholm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shirley_Chisholm" title="Shirley Chisholm">Shirley Chisholm</a> was the first major-party African American candidate to run nationwide primary campaigns.</div></div></div>
<p>The modern Democratic party emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_equality" title="Social equality">social equality</a> through liberalism. They support <a href="/wiki/Voting_rights_in_the_United_States" title="Voting rights in the United States">voting rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minority_rights" title="Minority rights">minority rights</a>, including <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_States" title="LGBT rights in the United States">LGBT rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">religious secularism</a>. A longstanding social policy is upholding <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a>, which affect ethnic and racial minorities and includes voting rights, <a href="/wiki/Equal_opportunity" title="Equal opportunity">equal opportunity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racial_equality" title="Racial equality">racial equality</a>. The party championed the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>, which for the first time outlawed segregation. Democrats made civil rights and <a href="/wiki/Anti-racism" title="Anti-racism">anti-racism</a> a core party philosophy. Carmines and Stimson say that "the Democratic Party appropriated racial liberalism and assumed federal responsibility for ending racial discrimination".<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ideological social elements in the party include <a href="/wiki/Cultural_liberalism" title="Cultural liberalism">cultural liberalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civil_libertarianism" title="Civil libertarianism">civil libertarianism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminism</a>. Other Democratic social policies are <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">internationalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Open_immigration" class="mw-redirect" title="Open immigration">open immigration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_reform" title="Electoral reform">electoral reform</a> and women's <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">reproductive rights</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Equal_opportunity">Equal opportunity</span></h4>
<p>The Democratic Party supports <a href="/wiki/Equal_opportunity" title="Equal opportunity">equal opportunity</a> for all Americans regardless of sex, age, race, ethnicity, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a>, religion, creed, or national origin. Many Democrats support <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> programs to further this goal. Democrats also strongly support the <a href="/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act_of_1990" title="Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990">Americans with Disabilities Act</a> to prohibit discrimination against people based on physical or mental disability. As such, the Democrats pushed as well the <a href="/wiki/ADA_Amendments_Act_of_2008" title="ADA Amendments Act of 2008">ADA Amendments Act of 2008</a>, a legal expansion that became law.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Voting_rights">Voting rights</span></h4>
<p>The party is very supportive of improving voting rights as well as election accuracy and accessibility.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> They support ending <a href="/wiki/Voter_ID_laws_in_the_United_States" title="Voter ID laws in the United States">voter ID laws</a> and increasing voting time, including making election day a holiday. They support reforming the electoral system to eliminate <a href="/wiki/Gerrymandering" title="Gerrymandering">gerrymandering</a> as well as passing comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Campaign_finance_reform_in_the_United_States" title="Campaign finance reform in the United States">campaign finance reform</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ontheissues.org_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ontheissues.org-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> They supported the <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">Voting Rights Act of 1965</a> and as a party have often been pioneers for democracy in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion_and_reproductive_rights">Abortion and reproductive rights</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Abortion_law_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Abortion law in the United States">Abortion law in the United States</a></div>
<p>The Democratic Party believe that all women should have access to <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a> and support public funding of contraception for poor women. In its national platforms from 1992 to 2004, the Democratic Party has called for <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a> to be "safe, legal and rare"—namely, keeping it legal by rejecting laws that allow governmental interference in abortion decisions and reducing the number of abortions by promoting both knowledge of reproduction and contraception and incentives for adoption. The wording changed in the 2008 platform. When Congress voted on the <a href="/wiki/Partial-Birth_Abortion_Ban_Act" title="Partial-Birth Abortion Ban Act">Partial-Birth Abortion Ban Act</a> in 2003, Congressional Democrats were split, with a minority (including former <a href="/wiki/Party_leaders_of_the_United_States_Senate" title="Party leaders of the United States Senate">Senate Majority Leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">Harry Reid</a>) supporting the ban and the majority of Democrats opposing the legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Democratic Party opposes attempts to reverse the 1973 Supreme Court decision <i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i>, which declared abortion covered by the constitutionally protected individual <a href="/wiki/Right_to_privacy" title="Right to privacy">right to privacy</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Ninth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Ninth Amendment</a>; and <i><a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood_v._Casey" title="Planned Parenthood v. Casey">Planned Parenthood v. Casey</a></i>, which lays out the legal framework in which government action alleged to violate that right is assessed by courts. As a matter of the <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">right to privacy</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, many Democrats believe all women should have the ability to choose to abort without governmental interference. They believe that each woman, conferring with her conscience, has the right to choose for herself whether abortion is morally correct.
</p><p>Former <a href="/wiki/Party_leaders_of_the_United_States_Senate" title="Party leaders of the United States Senate">Senate Minority Leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">Harry Reid</a> identified himself as "<a href="/wiki/Pro-life" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-life">pro-life</a>", Former President <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> has expressed his view of abortion and his wish to see the Democratic Party becoming more <a href="/wiki/Anti-abortion_movements" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-abortion movements">pro-life</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> while President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker of the House</a> <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi" title="Nancy Pelosi">Nancy Pelosi</a> self-identify as "<a href="/wiki/Pro-choice" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-choice">pro-choice</a>". Groups such as <a href="/wiki/Democrats_for_Life_of_America" title="Democrats for Life of America">Democrats for Life of America</a> represent the pro-life <a href="/wiki/Political_faction" title="Political faction">faction</a> of the party while groups such as <a href="/wiki/EMILY%27s_List" title="EMILY&#39;s List">EMILY's List</a> represent the pro-choice <a href="/wiki/Political_faction" title="Political faction">faction</a>. A <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> poll from October 2006 found that 25% of Democrats were pro-life while a 69% majority was pro-choice.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2016 Democratic Party platform expresses support for "'a woman’s right to safe and legal abortion' and enumerates no limits on that right."<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> It further calls for the repeal of the Hyde Amendment, which prohibits the use of federal tax dollars for elective abortions.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">Immigration to the United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">Illegal immigration to the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg/350px-Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg/525px-Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg/700px-Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Immigration_Bill_Signing_-_A1421-33a_-_10-03-1965.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Lyndon B. Johnson signs the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1965" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration Act of 1965">Immigration Act of 1965</a> as <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Humphrey" title="Hubert Humphrey">Hubert Humphrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senators</a> <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Edward M. Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> and others look on.</div></div></div>
<p>Many Democratic politicians have called for systematic reform of the immigration system such that residents that have <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">come into the United States illegally</a> have a pathway to legal citizenship. President Obama remarked in November 2013 that he felt it was "long past time to fix our broken immigration system", particularly to allow "incredibly bright young people" that came over as students to become full citizens. The Public Religion Research Institute found in a late 2013 study that 73% of Democrats supported the pathway concept, compared to 63% of Americans as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-long-past_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-long-past-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Democrats in the Senate passed <a href="/wiki/Border_Security,_Economic_Opportunity,_and_Immigration_Modernization_Act_of_2013" title="Border Security, Economic Opportunity, and Immigration Modernization Act of 2013">S.744</a>, which would reform immigration policy to allow citizenship for illegal immigrants in the United States and improve the lives of all immigrants currently living in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span></h4>
<p>The Democratic Party is supportive of <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> rights. Most support for <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">same-sex marriage in the United States</a> has come from Democrats, although some favor <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> instead or oppose same-sex marriage. Support for same-sex marriage has increased in the past decade according to <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a>. An April 2009 ABC News/<i>Washington Post</i> public opinion poll put support among Democrats at 62%<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> whereas a June 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> poll found that 42% of Democrats support same-sex marriage while 23% support <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> or <a href="/wiki/Domestic_partnership" title="Domestic partnership">domestic partnership</a> laws and 28% oppose any legal recognition at all.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> A broad majority of Democrats have supported other LGBT-related laws such as extending <a href="/wiki/Hate_crime" title="Hate crime">hate crime</a> statutes, <a href="/wiki/Employment_Non-Discrimination_Act" title="Employment Non-Discrimination Act">legally preventing discrimination against LGBT people in the workforce</a> and repealing <a href="/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell" title="Don&#39;t ask, don&#39;t tell">Don't ask, don't tell</a>. A 2006 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> poll of Democrats found that 55% supported gays adopting children with 40% opposed while 70% support <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation_and_military_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual orientation and military service">gays in the military</a>, with only 23% opposed.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Gallup polling from May 2009 stated that 82% of Democrats support open enlistment.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2004 Democratic National Platform stated that marriage should be defined at the state level and it repudiated the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Marriage_Amendment" title="Federal Marriage Amendment">Federal Marriage Amendment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-platform_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platform-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> While not stating support of same-sex marriage, the 2008 platform called for repeal of the <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act" title="Defense of Marriage Act">Defense of Marriage Act</a>, which banned federal recognition of same-sex marriage and removed the need for interstate recognition, supported antidiscrimination laws and the extension of hate crime laws to LGBT people and opposed the Don't ask, don't tell military policy.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The 2012 platform included support for same-sex marriage and for the repeal of DOMA.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 9, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> became the first sitting President to say he supports same-sex marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Huffington_Post_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Huffington_Post-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Previously, he had opposed restrictions on same-sex marriage such as the <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act" title="Defense of Marriage Act">Defense of Marriage Act</a>, which he promised to repeal,<sup id="cite_ref-LGBT_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGBT-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Prop_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Prop 8">Prop 8</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_amendment" title="Constitutional amendment">constitutional amendment</a> to ban same-sex marriage (which he opposed saying that "decisions about marriage should be left to the states as they always have been"),<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> but also stated that he personally believed marriage to be between a man and a woman and that he favored civil unions that would "give same-sex couples equal legal rights and privileges as married couples".<sup id="cite_ref-LGBT_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGBT-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Earlier, when running for the Illinois Senate in 1996 he said that he "unequivocally support(ed) gay marriage" and "favor(ed) legalizing same-sex marriages, and would fight efforts to prohibit such marriages".<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, Democratic presidential candidate in 2004, did not support same-sex marriage. Former presidents <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and former Vice Presidents <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Mondale" title="Walter Mondale">Walter Mondale</a><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> also support gay marriage.
</p>
<h4><span id="Civil_Rights_.E2.80.93_United_States_Citizens_in_Puerto_Rico"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_Rights_–_United_States_Citizens_in_Puerto_Rico">Civil Rights – United States Citizens in Puerto Rico</span></h4>
<p>The 2016 Democratic Party platform declares: "We are committed to addressing the extraordinary challenges faced by our fellow citizens in Puerto Rico. Many stem from the fundamental question of Puerto Rico's political status. Democrats believe that the people of Puerto Rico should determine their ultimate political status from permanent options that do not conflict with the Constitution, laws, and policies of the United States. Democrats are committed to promoting economic opportunity and good-paying jobs for the hardworking people of Puerto Rico. We also believe that Puerto Ricans must be treated equally by Medicare, Medicaid, and other programs that benefit families. Puerto Ricans should be able to vote for the people who make their laws, just as they should be treated equally. All American citizens, no matter where they reside, should have the right to vote for the President of the United States. Finally, we believe that federal officials must respect Puerto Rico's local self-government as laws are implemented and Puerto Rico's budget and debt are restructured so that it can get on a path towards stability and prosperity".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gun_control">Gun control</span></h4>
<p>With a stated goal of reducing crime and homicide, the Democratic Party has introduced various <a href="/wiki/Gun_politics_in_the_United_States" title="Gun politics in the United States">gun control</a> measures, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Gun_Control_Act_of_1968" title="Gun Control Act of 1968">Gun Control Act of 1968</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brady_Handgun_Violence_Prevention_Act" title="Brady Handgun Violence Prevention Act">Brady Bill</a> of 1993 and Crime Control Act of 1994. However, some Democrats, especially rural, Southern, and Western Democrats, favor fewer restrictions on firearm possession and warned the party was defeated in the 2000 presidential election in rural areas because of the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In the national platform for 2008, the only statement explicitly favoring gun control was a plan calling for renewal of the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assault_Weapons_Ban" title="Federal Assault Weapons Ban">Assault Weapons Ban</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_penalty">Death penalty</span></h4>
<p>The Democratic Party supports the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a> far less than the Republican Party. Although most Democrats in Congress have never seriously moved to overturn the rarely used <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_by_the_United_States_federal_government" title="Capital punishment by the United States federal government">federal death penalty</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Russ_Feingold" title="Russ Feingold">Russ Feingold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Kucinich" title="Dennis Kucinich">Dennis Kucinich</a> have introduced such bills with little success. Democrats have led efforts to overturn state death penalty laws, particularly in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey#Capital_punishment" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> and in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>. They have also sought to prevent the reinstatement of the death penalty in those states which prohibit it, including Massachusetts and <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)#Capital_punishment" title="New York (state)">New York</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Presidency of Bill Clinton">Clinton administration</a>, Democrats led the expansion of the federal death penalty. These efforts resulted in the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Antiterrorism_and_Effective_Death_Penalty_Act_of_1996" title="Antiterrorism and Effective Death Penalty Act of 1996">Antiterrorism and Effective Death Penalty Act of 1996</a>, signed into law by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">President Clinton</a>, which heavily limited appeals in death penalty cases.
</p><p>In 1992, 1993 and 1995, Democratic Texas Congressman <a href="/wiki/Henry_B._Gonzalez" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry B. Gonzalez">Henry González</a> unsuccessfully introduced the <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Death_Penalty_Abolition_Amendment" class="extiw" title="s:Death Penalty Abolition Amendment">Death Penalty Abolition Amendment</a> which prohibited the use of <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_United_States" title="Capital punishment in the United States">capital punishment in the United States</a>. Democratic Missouri Congressman <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clay" title="Bill Clay">William Lacy Clay, Sr.</a> cosponsored the amendment in 1993.
</p><p>During his <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Senate_career_of_Barack_Obama" title="Illinois Senate career of Barack Obama">Illinois Senate career</a>, former <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> successfully introduced legislation intended to reduce the likelihood of <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage_of_justice" title="Miscarriage of justice">wrongful convictions</a> in capital cases, requiring videotaping of confessions. When <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2008">campaigning for the presidency</a>, Obama stated that he supports the limited use of the death penalty, including for people who have been convicted of raping a minor under the age of 12, having opposed the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a>'s ruling in <i><a href="/wiki/Kennedy_v._Louisiana" title="Kennedy v. Louisiana">Kennedy v. Louisiana</a></i> that the death penalty was unconstitutional in child rape cases.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Obama has stated that he thinks the "death penalty does little to deter crime" and that it is used too frequently and too inconsistently.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2016, the Democratic Platform Drafting Committee unanimously adopted an amendment to abolish the death penalty, marking the first time the party had done so in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Torture">Torture</span></h4>
<p>Many Democrats are opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Torture_and_the_United_States" title="Torture and the United States">use of torture</a> against individuals apprehended and held prisoner by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="United States armed forces">United States military</a> and hold that categorizing such prisoners as <a href="/wiki/Unlawful_combatant" title="Unlawful combatant">unlawful combatants</a> does not release the United States from its obligations under the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a>. Democrats contend that torture is inhumane, decreases the United States' moral standing in the world and produces questionable results. Democrats largely spoke out against <a href="/wiki/Waterboarding" title="Waterboarding">waterboarding</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Torture became a very divisive issue in the party after Barack Obama was elected President.
